</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Legislature</th><td><a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Morocco" title="Parliament of Morocco">Parliament</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div </div></th><td>788</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">•&#160;<a href="/wiki/Alaouite_dynasty" title="Alaouite March 1912</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">•&#160;<a </ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Morocco</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/ɒ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;body&#39;">ɒ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span></span>/</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Morocco.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/34/En-us-Morocco.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Morocco.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">المغرب</span>&#8206;, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">romanized</a>:&#160;</small><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">al-maġhrib</i>, <small><a href="/wiki/Literal_translation" title="Literal translation">lit.</a>&#160;</small>&#39;place the sun sets; the west&#39;; <a href="/wiki/Standard_Moroccan_Tamazight_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Moroccan Tamazight language">Standard Moroccan Tamazight</a>: <span lang="zgh">ⵍⵎⵖⵔⵉⴱ</span>, <small>romanized:&#160;</small><i lang="zgh-Latn" title="Standard Moroccan Tamazight-language romanization">lmeɣrib</i>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Maroc</i>), officially the <b>Kingdom of Morocco</b> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">المملكة المغربية</span>&#8206;, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">romanized</a>:&#160;</small><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">al-mamlakah al-maghribiyah</i>, <small><a href="/wiki/Literal_translation" title="Literal translation">lit.</a>&#160;</small>&#39;The Western Kingdom&#39;; <a href="/wiki/Standard_Moroccan_Tamazight_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Moroccan Tamazight language">Standard Moroccan Tamazight</a>: <span lang="zgh">ⵜⴰⴳⵍⴷⵉⵜ ⵏ ⵍⵎⵖⵔⵉⴱ</span>, <small>romanized:&#160;</small><i lang="zgh-Latn" title="Standard Moroccan Tamazight-language romanization">tageldit n lmaɣrib</i>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Royaume du Maroc</i>), is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> located in the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a> region of <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>.  It overlooks the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> to the north and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> to the west. Morocco claims the areas of <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pe%C3%B1%C3%B3n_de_V%C3%A9lez_de_la_Gomera" title="Peñón de Vélez de la Gomera">Peñón de Vélez de la Gomera</a>, all of them under <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spanish</a> jurisdiction.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The capital is <a href="/wiki/Rabat" title="Rabat">Rabat</a> and the largest city <a href="/wiki/Casablanca" title="Casablanca">Casablanca</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Abun-Nasr1987_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abun-Nasr1987-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Morocco spans an area of 710,850&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (274,460&#160;sq&#160;mi) and has a population of over 35 million.
</p><p>Since the foundation of the <a href="/wiki/Idrisid_dynasty" title="Idrisid dynasty">first Moroccan state</a> by <a href="/wiki/Idris_I_of_Morocco" title="Idris I of Morocco">Idris I</a> in 788 AD, the country has been ruled by a series of independent dynasties, reaching its zenith under <a href="/wiki/Almoravid_dynasty" title="Almoravid dynasty">Almoravid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Almohad_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Almohad dynasty">Almohad</a> rule, when it spanned parts of <a href="/wiki/Iberia" class="mw-redirect" title="Iberia">Iberia</a> and northwestern Africa. The <a href="/wiki/Marinid_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Marinid dynasty">Marinid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saadi_dynasty" title="Saadi dynasty">Saadi</a> dynasties resisted foreign domination into the 17th century, allowing Morocco to remain the only northwest African country to avoid <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> occupation. The <a href="/wiki/Alaouite_dynasty" title="Alaouite dynasty">Alaouite dynasty</a>, which rules to this day, seized power in 1631. The country's strategic location near the mouth of the Mediterranean attracted Europeans interest, and in 1912, Morocco was divided into <a href="/wiki/French_Morocco" class="mw-redirect" title="French Morocco">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Morocco" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Morocco">Spanish</a> protectorates, with an <a href="/wiki/Tangier_International_Zone" title="Tangier International Zone">international zone in Tangier</a>. It regained its independence in 1956, and has since remained comparatively stable and prosperous by regional standards, with the fifth largest economy in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Morocco claims the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_Non-Self-Governing_Territories" title="United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories">non-self-governing territory</a> of <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a>, formerly <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Sahara" title="Spanish Sahara">Spanish Sahara</a>, as its <a href="/wiki/Southern_Provinces" title="Southern Provinces">Southern Provinces</a>. After Spain <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Accords" title="Madrid Accords">agreed to decolonise the territory</a> to Morocco and <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a> in 1975, <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara_War" title="Western Sahara War">a guerrilla war</a> arose with <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_people" title="Sahrawi people">local</a> forces. Mauritania relinquished <a href="/wiki/Tiris_al-Gharbiyya" title="Tiris al-Gharbiyya">its claim</a> in 1979, and the war lasted until a ceasefire in 1991. Morocco currently occupies two thirds of the territory, and <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara_peace_process" title="Western Sahara peace process">peace processes</a> have thus far failed to break the political deadlock.
</p><p>Morocco is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> with an elected parliament. The country wields significant influence in both Africa and the Arab world, and  is considered a <a href="/wiki/Regional_power" title="Regional power">regional power</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Middle_power" title="Middle power">middle power</a>. The <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_Morocco" title="List of rulers of Morocco">King of Morocco</a> holds vast executive and legislative powers, especially over the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Morocco" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Morocco">military</a>, foreign policy and religious affairs. <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the <a href="/wiki/Moroccan_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Moroccan government">government</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislative power</a> is vested in both the government and the two chambers of parliament, the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_Representatives_of_Morocco" class="mw-redirect" title="Assembly of Representatives of Morocco">Assembly of Representatives</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_Councillors" class="mw-redirect" title="Assembly of Councillors">Assembly of Councillors</a>. The king can issue decrees called <a href="/wiki/Moroccan_Dahir" title="Moroccan Dahir">dahirs</a>, which have the force of law. He can also dissolve the parliament after consulting the <a href="/wiki/List_of_heads_of_government_of_Morocco" title="List of heads of government of Morocco">Prime Minister</a> and the president of the constitutional court.
</p><p>Morocco's predominant religion is <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, and its official languages are <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Berber</a>, the latter achieving official recognition in 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> having been the native language of Morocco before the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_the_Maghreb" title="Muslim conquest of the Maghreb">Muslim conquest</a> in the seventh century C.E.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Moroccan_dialect" class="mw-redirect" title="Moroccan dialect">Moroccan dialect</a> of Arabic, referred to as <i>Darija</i>, and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> are also widely spoken. Moroccan culture is a blend of <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">Berber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">Sephardi Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_African" class="mw-redirect" title="West African">West African</a> and European influences.
</p><p>Morocco is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Union_for_the_Mediterranean" title="Union for the Mediterranean">Union for the Mediterranean</a> and the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<p>The full <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> name <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">al-Mamlakah al-Maghribiyyah</i></i> (<span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic language text">المملكة المغربية</span>) translates to "Kingdom of the West"; although "the West" in Arabic is <span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic language text">الغرب</span> <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">Al-Gharb</i></i>. For historical references, medieval Arab historians and geographers sometimes referred to Morocco as <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">al-Maghrib al-Aqṣá</i></i> (<span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic language text">المغرب الأقصى</span>, meaning "The Farthest West") to distinguish it from neighbouring historical regions called <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">al-Maghrib al-Awsaṭ</i></i> (<span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic language text">المغرب الأوسط</span>, meaning "<a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">The Middle West</a>") and <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">al-Maghrib al-Adná</i></i> (<span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic language text">المغرب الأدنى</span>, meaning "<a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">The Nearest West</a>").<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Morocco's English name is based on <a href="/wiki/Marrakesh" title="Marrakesh">Marrakesh</a>, its capital under the <a href="/wiki/Almoravid_dynasty" title="Almoravid dynasty">Almoravid dynasty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Almohad_Caliphate" title="Almohad Caliphate">Almohad Caliphate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The origin of the name Marrakesh is disputed,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> but is most likely from the <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Berber</a> words <i>amur (n) akush</i> (ⴰⵎⵓⵔ ⵏ ⴰⴽⵓⵛ) or "Land of God".<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The modern Berber name for Marrakesh is <i>Mṛṛakc</i> (in the <a href="/wiki/Berber_Latin_alphabet" title="Berber Latin alphabet">Berber Latin script</a>). In <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>, Morocco is known as <i>Fas</i>, a name derived from its ancient capital of <a href="/wiki/Fes" class="mw-redirect" title="Fes">Fes</a>. However, this was not the case in other parts of the Islamic world: until the middle of the 20th century, the common name of Morocco in Egyptian and Middle Eastern Arabic literature was <i>Marrakesh</i> (مراكش);<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> this name is still used in some languages such as <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_language" title="Punjabi language">Punjabi</a>. The English name Morocco is an <a href="/wiki/Anglicisation" title="Anglicisation">anglicisation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> "Marruecos", from which also derives the <a href="/wiki/Tuscan_dialect" title="Tuscan dialect">Tuscan</a> "Morrocco", the origin of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> "Marocco".
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Morocco" title="History of Morocco">History of Morocco</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory_and_antiquity">Prehistory and antiquity</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ptolemy_of_Mauretania_Louvre_Ma1887.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Ptolemy_of_Mauretania_Louvre_Ma1887.jpg/180px-Ptolemy_of_Mauretania_Louvre_Ma1887.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="273" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Ptolemy_of_Mauretania_Louvre_Ma1887.jpg/270px-Ptolemy_of_Mauretania_Louvre_Ma1887.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Ptolemy_of_Mauretania_Louvre_Ma1887.jpg/360px-Ptolemy_of_Mauretania_Louvre_Ma1887.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="3636" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ptolemy_of_Mauretania_Louvre_Ma1887.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Berber Roman client King <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy_of_Mauretania" title="Ptolemy of Mauretania">Ptolemy of Mauretania</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The area of present-day Morocco has been inhabited since <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic times</a>, sometime between 190,000 and 90,000&#160;BC.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>  A recent publication may demonstrate an even earlier habitation period, as <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens">Homo sapiens</a></i> fossils discovered in the late 2000s near the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic coast</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jebel_Irhoud" title="Jebel Irhoud">Jebel Irhoud</a> were recently dated to roughly 315,000 years before present.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>  During the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Paleolithic" title="Upper Paleolithic">Upper Paleolithic</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a> was more fertile than it is today, resembling a <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savanna</a> more than today's arid landscape.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Twenty-two thousand years ago, the <a href="/wiki/Aterian" title="Aterian">Aterian</a> was succeeded by the <a href="/wiki/Iberomaurusian" title="Iberomaurusian">Iberomaurusian</a> culture, which shared similarities with Iberian cultures. Skeletal similarities have been suggested between the <a href="/wiki/Iberomaurusian" title="Iberomaurusian">Iberomaurusian</a> "<a href="/wiki/Mechta-Afalou" title="Mechta-Afalou">Mechta-Afalou</a>" burials and European <a href="/wiki/Cro-Magnon" class="mw-redirect" title="Cro-Magnon">Cro-Magnon</a> remains. The Iberomaurusian was succeeded by the <a href="/wiki/Beaker_culture" title="Beaker culture">Beaker culture</a> in Morocco.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mitochondrial_DNA" title="Mitochondrial DNA">Mitochondrial DNA</a> studies have discovered a close link between <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">Berbers</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sami_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Sami people">Saami</a> of Scandinavia. This supports theories that the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Cantabrian_region" title="Franco-Cantabrian region">Franco-Cantabrian refuge area of southwestern Europe</a> was the source of late-glacial expansions of hunter-gatherers who repopulated northern Europe after the last <a href="/wiki/Ice_age" title="Ice age">ice age</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Northwest Africa and Morocco were slowly drawn into the wider emerging <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediterranean">Mediterranean</a> world by the <a href="/wiki/Phoenicians" class="mw-redirect" title="Phoenicians">Phoenicians</a>, who established trading colonies and settlements in the early Classical period. Substantial Phoenician settlements were at <a href="/wiki/Chellah" title="Chellah">Chellah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lixus_(ancient_city)" title="Lixus (ancient city)">Lixus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mogador" class="mw-redirect" title="Mogador">Mogador</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Mogador was a Phoenician colony as early as the early 6th century BC.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (February 2013)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Volubilis_Longshot_II.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Volubilis_Longshot_II.jpg/200px-Volubilis_Longshot_II.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Volubilis_Longshot_II.jpg/300px-Volubilis_Longshot_II.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Volubilis_Longshot_II.jpg/400px-Volubilis_Longshot_II.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1280" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Volubilis_Longshot_II.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ancient Roman ruins of <a href="/wiki/Volubilis" title="Volubilis">Volubilis</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Morocco later became a realm of the Northwest African civilisation of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Carthage" title="Ancient Carthage">ancient Carthage</a> as part of its empire. The earliest known independent Moroccan state was the <a href="/wiki/Mauretania" title="Mauretania">Berber kingdom of Mauretania</a> under king <a href="/wiki/Baga_(king)" title="Baga (king)">Baga</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> This ancient kingdom (not to be confused with the present state of <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a>) dates at least to around 225&#160;BC.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mauretania" title="Mauretania">Mauretania</a> became a <a href="/wiki/Client_state" title="Client state">client</a> kingdom of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> in 33 BC. Emperor <a href="/wiki/Claudius" title="Claudius">Claudius</a> annexed Mauretania directly as a <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">Roman province</a> in 44 AD, under an imperial <a href="/wiki/Governor" title="Governor">governor</a> (either a<i>procurator Augusti</i>, or a <i>legatus Augusti pro praetore</i>).
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Crisis_of_the_3rd_century" class="mw-redirect" title="Crisis of the 3rd century">crisis of the 3rd century</a>, parts of Mauretania were reconquered by Berber tribes. Direct Roman rule became confined to a few coastal cities, such as Septum (<a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a>) in <a href="/wiki/Mauretania_Tingitana" title="Mauretania Tingitana">Mauretania Tingitana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cherchell" title="Cherchell">Cherchell</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mauretania_Caesariensis" title="Mauretania Caesariensis">Mauretania Caesariensis</a>, by the late 3rd century. The Roman Empire lost its remaining possessions in Mauretania after the area was devastated by the <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a> in AD 429. After this point, local Mauro-Roman kings assumed control (see <a href="/wiki/Mauro-Roman_kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Mauro-Roman kingdom">Mauro-Roman kingdom</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Roman Empire">Eastern Roman Empire</a> under Byzantine control re-established direct imperial rule of Septum and <a href="/wiki/Tingi" title="Tingi">Tingi</a> in the 530s. Tingis was fortified and a church erected.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation_and_early_Islamic_era">Foundation and early Islamic era</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Idrisid_dynasty" title="Idrisid dynasty">Idrisid dynasty</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Idrisids_coin_minted_at_Al_Aliyah_Morocco_840_CE.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Idrisids_coin_minted_at_Al_Aliyah_Morocco_840_CE.jpg/190px-Idrisids_coin_minted_at_Al_Aliyah_Morocco_840_CE.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Idrisids_coin_minted_at_Al_Aliyah_Morocco_840_CE.jpg/285px-Idrisids_coin_minted_at_Al_Aliyah_Morocco_840_CE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Idrisids_coin_minted_at_Al_Aliyah_Morocco_840_CE.jpg/380px-Idrisids_coin_minted_at_Al_Aliyah_Morocco_840_CE.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1437" data-file-height="1412" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Idrisids_coin_minted_at_Al_Aliyah_Morocco_840_CE.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Idrisid_dynasty" title="Idrisid dynasty">Idrisid</a> coin, minted at al-'Aliyah (<a href="/wiki/Fez,_Morocco" title="Fez, Morocco">Fes</a>), Morocco, 840 CE.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_the_Maghreb" title="Muslim conquest of the Maghreb">Muslim conquest of the Maghreb</a>, that started in the middle of the 7th century, was <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_the_Maghreb#Completion_of_the_conquest" title="Muslim conquest of the Maghreb">achieved</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyad Caliphate</a> early into the following century. It brought both the Arabic language and <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> to the area. Although part of the larger <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">Islamic Empire</a>, Morocco was initially organized as a subsidiary province of <a href="/wiki/Ifriqiya" title="Ifriqiya">Ifriqiya</a>, with the local governors appointed by the Muslim governor in <a href="/wiki/Kairouan" title="Kairouan">Kairouan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The indigenous Berber tribes adopted Islam, but retained their <a href="/wiki/Customary_law" title="Customary law">customary laws</a>. They also paid taxes and tribute to the new Muslim administration.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The first independent Muslim state in the area of modern Morocco was the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Nekor" title="Kingdom of Nekor">Kingdom of Nekor</a>, an emirate in the <a href="/wiki/Rif_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Rif Mountains">Rif Mountains</a>. It was founded by <a href="/wiki/Salih_I_ibn_Mansur" title="Salih I ibn Mansur">Salih I ibn Mansur</a> in 710, as a client state to the Umayyad Caliphate. After the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Berber_Revolt" title="Berber Revolt">Berber Revolt</a> in 739, the Berbers formed other independent states such as the <a href="/wiki/Miknasa" title="Miknasa">Miknasa</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sijilmasa" title="Sijilmasa">Sijilmasa</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Barghawata" title="Barghawata">Barghawata</a>.
</p><p>According to medieval legend, <a href="/wiki/Idris_I_of_Morocco" title="Idris I of Morocco">Idris ibn Abdallah</a> had fled to Morocco after the <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasids</a>' massacre of his tribe in Iraq. He convinced the Awraba Berber tribes to break their allegiance to the distant Abbasid caliphs in <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a> and he founded the <a href="/wiki/Idrisid_dynasty" title="Idrisid dynasty">Idrisid dynasty</a> in 788. The Idrisids established <a href="/wiki/Fes,_Morocco" class="mw-redirect" title="Fes, Morocco">Fes</a> as their capital and Morocco became a centre of Muslim learning and a major <a href="/wiki/Regional_power" title="Regional power">regional power</a>. The Idrissids were ousted in 927 by the <a href="/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate" title="Fatimid Caliphate">Fatimid Caliphate</a> and their Miknasa allies. After Miknasa broke off relations with the Fatimids in 932, they were removed from power by the <a href="/wiki/Maghrawa" title="Maghrawa">Maghrawa</a> of Sijilmasa in 980.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dynasties">Dynasties</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Empire_almohade.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Empire_almohade.PNG/220px-Empire_almohade.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Empire_almohade.PNG/330px-Empire_almohade.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Empire_almohade.PNG/440px-Empire_almohade.PNG 2x" data-file-width="882" data-file-height="648" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Empire_almohade.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Almohad_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Almohad dynasty">Almohad</a> realm at its greatest extent, c. 1212</div></div></div>
<p>From the 11th century onwards, a series of Berber dynasties arose.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Under the <a href="/wiki/Almoravid_dynasty" title="Almoravid dynasty">Almoravid dynasty</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Almohad_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Almohad dynasty">Almohad dynasty</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Morocco dominated the Maghreb, much of present-day Spain and Portugal, and the western Mediterranean region. From the 13th century onwards the country saw a massive migration of the <a href="/wiki/Banu_Hilal" title="Banu Hilal">Banu Hilal</a> Arab tribes. In the 13th and 14th centuries the <a href="/wiki/Merinid_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Merinid Dynasty">Merinids</a> held power in Morocco and strove to replicate the successes of the <a href="/wiki/Almohad_Caliphate" title="Almohad Caliphate">Almohads</a> by military campaigns in Algeria and Spain. They were followed by the <a href="/wiki/Wattasid_dynasty" title="Wattasid dynasty">Wattasids</a>. In the 15th century, the <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a> ended Muslim rule in central and southern <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and many <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Morocco" title="History of the Jews in Morocco">Jews</a> fled to Morocco.<sup id="cite_ref-brit_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brit-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> efforts to control the Atlantic sea trade in the 15th century did not greatly affect the interior of Morocco even though they managed to control some possessions on the Moroccan coast but not venturing further afield inland.
</p><p>On another note and according to Elizabeth Allo Isichei, "In 1520, there was a <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famine</a> in Morocco so terrible that for a long time other events were dated by it. It has been suggested that the population of Morocco fell from 5 to under 3&#160;million between the early sixteenth and nineteenth centuries."<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sharifian_dynasties">Sharifian dynasties</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ashraf" title="Ashraf">Ashraf</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Morocco,_Safi_ceramic_vessel_Jobbana.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Morocco%2C_Safi_ceramic_vessel_Jobbana.JPG/180px-Morocco%2C_Safi_ceramic_vessel_Jobbana.JPG" decoding="async" width="180" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Morocco%2C_Safi_ceramic_vessel_Jobbana.JPG/270px-Morocco%2C_Safi_ceramic_vessel_Jobbana.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Morocco%2C_Safi_ceramic_vessel_Jobbana.JPG/360px-Morocco%2C_Safi_ceramic_vessel_Jobbana.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2056" data-file-height="2831" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Morocco,_Safi_ceramic_vessel_Jobbana.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Morocco, Safi ceramic vessel Jobbana</div></div></div>
<p>In 1549, the region fell to successive Arab dynasties claiming descent from the <a href="/wiki/Prophets_in_Islam" class="mw-redirect" title="Prophets in Islam">Islamic prophet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a>: first the <a href="/wiki/Saadi_dynasty" title="Saadi dynasty">Saadi dynasty</a> who ruled from 1549 to 1659, and then the <a href="/wiki/Alaouite_dynasty" title="Alaouite dynasty">Alaouite dynasty</a>, who remain in power since the 17th century.
</p><p>Under the Saadi dynasty, the country repulsed <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> incursions and a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese</a> invasion at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ksar_el_Kebir" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Ksar el Kebir">battle of Ksar el Kebir</a> in 1578. The reign of <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_al-Mansur" title="Ahmad al-Mansur">Ahmad al-Mansur</a> brought new wealth and prestige to the Sultanate, and a large expedition to West Africa inflicted a crushing defeat on the <a href="/wiki/Songhay_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Songhay Empire">Songhay Empire</a> in 1591. However, managing the territories across the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a> proved too difficult. After the death of al-Mansur, the country was divided among his sons.
</p><p>In 1631, Morocco was reunited by the Alaouite dynasty, who have been the ruling house of Morocco ever since. Morocco was facing aggression from <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and the Ottoman Empire allies pressing westward. The Alaouites succeeded in stabilising their position, and while the kingdom was smaller than previous ones in the region, it remained quite wealthy. Against the opposition of local tribes <a href="/wiki/Ismail_Ibn_Sharif" title="Ismail Ibn Sharif">Ismail Ibn Sharif</a> (1672–1727) began to create a unified state.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> With his Jaysh d'Ahl al-Rif (the <a href="/wiki/Riff" class="mw-redirect" title="Riff">Riffian</a> Army) he seized <a href="/wiki/English_Tangier" title="English Tangier">Tangier</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">English</a> in 1684 and drove the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish</a> from <a href="/wiki/Larache" title="Larache">Larache</a> in 1689. Portuguese abandoned <a href="/wiki/El_Jadida" title="El Jadida">Mazagão</a>, their last territory in Morocco, in 1769. However, the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Melilla_(1774)" title="Siege of Melilla (1774)">Siege of Melilla</a> against the Spanish ended in defeat in 1775.
</p><p>Morocco was the first nation to recognise the fledgling United States as an independent nation in 1777.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> In the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>, American merchant ships in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> were subject to attack by the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirates" title="Barbary pirates">Barbary pirates</a>. On 20 December 1777, Morocco's Sultan <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_III_of_Morocco" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohammed III of Morocco">Mohammed III</a> declared that American merchant ships would be under the protection of the sultanate and could thus enjoy safe passage. The <a href="/wiki/Moroccan%E2%80%93American_Treaty_of_Friendship" title="Moroccan–American Treaty of Friendship">Moroccan–American Treaty of Friendship</a>, signed in 1786, stands as the U.S.'s oldest non-broken friendship <a href="/wiki/Treaty" title="Treaty">treaty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_and_Spanish_protectorates:_1912_to_1956">French and Spanish protectorates: 1912 to 1956</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/French_protectorate_in_Morocco" title="French protectorate in Morocco">French protectorate in Morocco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Protectorate_in_Morocco" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Protectorate in Morocco">Spanish Protectorate in Morocco</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Forteresse_Jadida_03.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Forteresse_Jadida_03.JPG/220px-Forteresse_Jadida_03.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Forteresse_Jadida_03.JPG/330px-Forteresse_Jadida_03.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Forteresse_Jadida_03.JPG/440px-Forteresse_Jadida_03.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Forteresse_Jadida_03.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Former Portuguese <a href="/wiki/El_Jadida#Fortress_of_Mazagan" title="El Jadida">fortress of Mazagan</a> in <a href="/wiki/El_Jadida" title="El Jadida">El Jadida</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:War_in_Morocco_Death_of_Spanish_general_Margallo.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/War_in_Morocco_Death_of_Spanish_general_Margallo.JPG/220px-War_in_Morocco_Death_of_Spanish_general_Margallo.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/War_in_Morocco_Death_of_Spanish_general_Margallo.JPG/330px-War_in_Morocco_Death_of_Spanish_general_Margallo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/War_in_Morocco_Death_of_Spanish_general_Margallo.JPG/440px-War_in_Morocco_Death_of_Spanish_general_Margallo.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3125" data-file-height="3640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:War_in_Morocco_Death_of_Spanish_general_Margallo.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Death of <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spanish</a> general <a href="/wiki/Juan_Garc%C3%ADa_y_Margallo" title="Juan García y Margallo">Margallo</a> during the <a href="/wiki/First_Melillan_campaign" title="First Melillan campaign">Melilla War</a>. <a href="/wiki/Le_Petit_Journal_(newspaper)" title="Le Petit Journal (newspaper)">Le Petit Journal</a>, 13 November 1893.</div></div></div>
<p>As Europe industrialised, Northwest Africa was increasingly prized for its potential for colonisation. France showed a strong interest in Morocco as early as 1830, not only to protect the border of its Algerian territory, but also because of the strategic position of Morocco with coasts on the Mediterranean and the open Atlantic.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In 1860, a dispute over Spain's Ceuta enclave led Spain to declare war. Victorious Spain won a further enclave and an enlarged Ceuta in the settlement. In 1884, Spain created a protectorate in the coastal areas of Morocco.
</p><p>In 1904, France and Spain carved out zones of influence in Morocco. Recognition by the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> of France's <a href="/wiki/Sphere_of_influence" title="Sphere of influence">sphere of influence</a> provoked a strong reaction from the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a>; and a crisis loomed in 1905. The matter was resolved at the <a href="/wiki/Algeciras_Conference" title="Algeciras Conference">Algeciras Conference</a> in 1906. The <a href="/wiki/Agadir_Crisis" title="Agadir Crisis">Agadir Crisis</a> of 1911 increased tensions between European powers. The 1912 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Fez" title="Treaty of Fez">Treaty of Fez</a> made Morocco a <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a> of France, and triggered the <a href="/wiki/1912_Fez_riots" title="1912 Fez riots">1912 Fez riots</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hirschberg1981_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hirschberg1981-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Spain continued to operate its coastal protectorate. By the same treaty, Spain assumed the role of <a href="/wiki/Protecting_power" title="Protecting power">protecting power</a> over the northern and southern <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Saharan</a> zones.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Tens of thousands of colonists entered Morocco. Some bought up large amounts of the rich agricultural land, others organised the exploitation and modernisation of mines and harbours. Interest groups that formed among these elements continually pressured France to increase its control over Morocco – a control which was also made necessary by the continuous wars among Moroccan tribes, part of which had taken sides with the French since the beginning of the conquest. Governor general Marshall <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Lyautey" title="Hubert Lyautey">Hubert Lyautey</a> sincerely admired Moroccan culture and succeeded in imposing a joint Moroccan-French administration, while creating a modern school system. Several divisions of Moroccan soldiers (<a href="/wiki/Goumier" class="mw-redirect" title="Goumier">Goumiers</a> or regular troops and officers) served in the <a href="/wiki/French_army" class="mw-redirect" title="French army">French army</a> in both <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, and in the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Franquism" class="mw-redirect" title="Franquism">Nationalist Army</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a> and after (<i><a href="/wiki/Regulares" title="Regulares">Regulares</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The institution of <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a> was abolished in 1925.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Louis_Comfort_Tiffany_-_Market_day_outside_the_walls_of_Tangiers,_Morocco.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Louis_Comfort_Tiffany_-_Market_day_outside_the_walls_of_Tangiers%2C_Morocco.jpg/220px-Louis_Comfort_Tiffany_-_Market_day_outside_the_walls_of_Tangiers%2C_Morocco.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Louis_Comfort_Tiffany_-_Market_day_outside_the_walls_of_Tangiers%2C_Morocco.jpg/330px-Louis_Comfort_Tiffany_-_Market_day_outside_the_walls_of_Tangiers%2C_Morocco.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Louis_Comfort_Tiffany_-_Market_day_outside_the_walls_of_Tangiers%2C_Morocco.jpg/440px-Louis_Comfort_Tiffany_-_Market_day_outside_the_walls_of_Tangiers%2C_Morocco.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="903" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Louis_Comfort_Tiffany_-_Market_day_outside_the_walls_of_Tangiers,_Morocco.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tangier" title="Tangier">Tangier</a>'s population included 40,000 Muslims, 31,000 Europeans and 15,000 Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Between 1921 and 1926, a <a href="/wiki/Rif_War" title="Rif War">Berber uprising</a> in the Rif Mountains, led by <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ibn_%27Abd_al-Karim_al-Khattabi" class="mw-redirect" title="Muhammad Ibn &#39;Abd al-Karim al-Khattabi">Abd el-Krim</a>, led to the establishment of the Republic of the Rif. The Spanish lost more than 13,000 soldiers at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Annual" title="Battle of Annual">Annual</a> in July–August 1921.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The rebellion was eventually suppressed by French and Spanish troops.
</p><p>In 1943, the <a href="/wiki/Istiqlal_Party" title="Istiqlal Party">Istiqlal Party</a> (Independence Party) was founded to press for independence, with discreet US support. That party subsequently provided most of the leadership for the nationalist movement.
</p><p>France's exile of <a href="/wiki/Sultan_Mohammed_V" class="mw-redirect" title="Sultan Mohammed V">Sultan Mohammed V</a> in 1953 to <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> and his replacement by the unpopular <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Ben_Aarafa" title="Mohammed Ben Aarafa">Mohammed Ben Aarafa</a> sparked active opposition to the French and Spanish protectorates. The most notable violence occurred in <a href="/wiki/Oujda" title="Oujda">Oujda</a> where Moroccans attacked French and other European residents in the streets. France allowed Mohammed V to return in 1955, and the negotiations that led to Moroccan independence began the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In March 1956 the French protectorate was ended and Morocco regained its independence from France as the "Kingdom of Morocco". A month later Spain ceded most of its protectorate in Northern Morocco to the new state but kept its two coastal enclaves (<a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a>) on the Mediterranean coast. Sultan Mohammed became king in 1957.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-independence">Post-independence</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marokko_011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Marokko_011.jpg/220px-Marokko_011.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Marokko_011.jpg/330px-Marokko_011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Marokko_011.jpg/440px-Marokko_011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1942" data-file-height="1405" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marokko_011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Mausoleum_of_Mohammed_V" title="Mausoleum of Mohammed V">Mausoleum of Mohammed V</a> in Rabat.</div></div></div>
<p>Upon the death of Mohammed V, <a href="/wiki/Hassan_II_of_Morocco" title="Hassan II of Morocco">Hassan II</a> became King of Morocco on 3 March 1961. Morocco held its first <a href="/wiki/Moroccan_parliamentary_election,_1963" class="mw-redirect" title="Moroccan parliamentary election, 1963">general elections in 1963</a>. However, Hassan declared a state of emergency and suspended parliament in 1965. In 1971, there was a failed attempt to depose the king and establish a republic. A truth commission set up in 2005 to investigate human rights abuses during his reign confirmed nearly 10,000 cases, ranging from death in detention to forced exile. Some 592 people were recorded killed during Hassan's rule according to the truth commission.
</p><p>The Spanish <a href="/wiki/Enclave" class="mw-redirect" title="Enclave">enclave</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ifni" title="Ifni">Ifni</a> in the south was returned to Morocco in 1969. The <a href="/wiki/Polisario_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Polisario movement">Polisario movement</a> was formed in 1973, with the aim of establishing an independent state in the Spanish Sahara. On 6 November 1975, King Hassan asked for volunteers to cross into the Spanish Sahara. Some 350,000 civilians were reported as being involved in the "<a href="/wiki/Green_March" title="Green March">Green March</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> A month later, Spain agreed to leave the Spanish Sahara, soon to become Western Sahara, and to transfer it to joint Moroccan-Mauritanian control, despite the objections and threats of military intervention by Algeria. Moroccan forces occupied the territory.<sup id="cite_ref-brit_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brit-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Moroccan and Algerian troops <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara_War" title="Western Sahara War">soon clashed in Western Sahara</a>. Morocco and Mauritania divided up Western Sahara. Fighting between the Moroccan military and Polisario forces continued for many years. The prolonged war was a considerable financial drain on Morocco. In 1983, Hassan cancelled planned elections amid political unrest and economic crisis. In 1984, Morocco left the Organisation of African Unity in protest at the <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic" title="Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic">SADR</a>'s admission to the body. Polisario claimed to have killed more than 5,000 Moroccan soldiers between 1982 and 1985.
</p><p>Algerian authorities have estimated the number of <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_refugees" title="Sahrawi refugees">Sahrawi refugees</a> in Algeria to be 165,000.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Diplomatic relations with Algeria were restored in 1988. In 1991, a UN-monitored ceasefire began in Western Sahara, but the territory's status remains undecided and ceasefire violations are reported. The following decade saw much wrangling over a proposed referendum on the future of the territory but the deadlock was not broken.
</p><p>Political reforms in the 1990s resulted in the establishment of a bicameral legislature in 1997 and Morocco's first opposition-led government came to power in 1998.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Les_Marocains_manifestent_pour_des_r%C3%A9formes_(5630977929).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Les_Marocains_manifestent_pour_des_r%C3%A9formes_%285630977929%29.jpg/220px-Les_Marocains_manifestent_pour_des_r%C3%A9formes_%285630977929%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Les_Marocains_manifestent_pour_des_r%C3%A9formes_%285630977929%29.jpg/330px-Les_Marocains_manifestent_pour_des_r%C3%A9formes_%285630977929%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Les_Marocains_manifestent_pour_des_r%C3%A9formes_%285630977929%29.jpg/440px-Les_Marocains_manifestent_pour_des_r%C3%A9formes_%285630977929%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="680" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Les_Marocains_manifestent_pour_des_r%C3%A9formes_(5630977929).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Protestors in <a href="/wiki/Casablanca" title="Casablanca">Casablanca</a> demand that authorities honor their promises of political reform.</div></div></div>
<p>King Hassan II died in 1999 and was succeeded by his son, <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_VI" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohammed VI">Mohammed VI</a>. He is a cautious moderniser who has introduced some economic and social liberalisation.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mohammed VI paid a controversial visit to the Western Sahara in 2002. Morocco unveiled an autonomy blueprint for Western Sahara to the United Nations in 2007. The Polisario rejected the plan and put forward its own proposal. Morocco and the Polisario Front held UN-sponsored talks in New York City but failed to come to any agreement. In 2010, security forces stormed a protest camp in the Western Sahara, triggering violent demonstrations in the regional capital <a href="/wiki/El_Aai%C3%BAn" class="mw-redirect" title="El Aaiún">El Aaiún</a>.
</p><p>In 2002, Morocco and Spain agreed to a US-brokered resolution over the disputed island of Perejil. Spanish troops had taken the normally uninhabited island after Moroccan soldiers landed on it and set up tents and a flag. There were renewed tensions in 2005, as hundreds of African migrants tried to storm the borders of the Spanish enclaves of Melilla and Ceuta. Morocco deported hundreds of the illegal migrants. In 2006, the Spanish Premier Zapatero visited Spanish enclaves. He was the first Spanish leader in 25 years to make an official visit to the territories. The following year, Spanish King <a href="/wiki/Juan_Carlos_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Juan Carlos I">Juan Carlos I</a> visited Ceuta and Melilla, further angering Morocco which demanded control of the enclaves.
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Moroccan_protests" title="2011–12 Moroccan protests">2011–12 Moroccan protests</a>, thousands of people rallied in Rabat and other cities calling for political reform and a new constitution curbing the powers of the king. In July 2011, the King won a landslide victory in a referendum on a reformed constitution he had proposed to placate the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a> protests. Despite the reforms made by Mohammed VI, demonstrators continued to call for deeper reforms. Hundreds took part in a trade union rally in Casablanca in May 2012. Participants accused the government of failing to deliver on reforms.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Morocco" title="Geography of Morocco">Geography of Morocco</a></div> 
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Atlas_Mountains_snow_cover.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Atlas_Mountains_snow_cover.jpg/220px-Atlas_Mountains_snow_cover.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Atlas_Mountains_snow_cover.jpg/330px-Atlas_Mountains_snow_cover.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Atlas_Mountains_snow_cover.jpg/440px-Atlas_Mountains_snow_cover.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Atlas_Mountains_snow_cover.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Toubkal" title="Toubkal">Toubkal</a>, the highest peak in Northwest Africa, at 4,167&#160;m (13,671&#160;ft)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chauen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Chauen.jpg/220px-Chauen.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Chauen.jpg/330px-Chauen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Chauen.jpg/440px-Chauen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4224" data-file-height="2376" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chauen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Rif" title="Rif">Rif</a> Mountains in northern Morocco</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_Djebel_el_Kest.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Panorama_Djebel_el_Kest.jpg/220px-Panorama_Djebel_el_Kest.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Panorama_Djebel_el_Kest.jpg/330px-Panorama_Djebel_el_Kest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Panorama_Djebel_el_Kest.jpg/440px-Panorama_Djebel_el_Kest.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6055" data-file-height="3145" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_Djebel_el_Kest.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A section of the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Atlas" title="Anti-Atlas">Anti-Atlas</a> near <a href="/wiki/Tafraout" title="Tafraout">Tafraout</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Moroccan_Atlantic_cedar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Moroccan_Atlantic_cedar.jpg/220px-Moroccan_Atlantic_cedar.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Moroccan_Atlantic_cedar.jpg/330px-Moroccan_Atlantic_cedar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Moroccan_Atlantic_cedar.jpg/440px-Moroccan_Atlantic_cedar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2292" data-file-height="3437" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Moroccan_Atlantic_cedar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An old <i><a href="/wiki/Cedrus_atlantica" title="Cedrus atlantica">Cedrus atlantica</a></i> tree in the Atlas range</div></div></div>
<p>Morocco has a coast by the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> that reaches past the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> to the north (a water border through the Strait and land borders with three small Spanish-controlled <a href="/wiki/Exclave" class="mw-redirect" title="Exclave">exclaves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pe%C3%B1%C3%B3n_de_V%C3%A9lez_de_la_Gomera" title="Peñón de Vélez de la Gomera">Peñón de Vélez de la Gomera</a>), <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> to the east, and <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a> to the south. Since Morocco controls most of Western Sahara, its <i>de facto</i> southern boundary is with <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a>.
</p><p>The internationally recognised borders of the country lie between latitudes <a href="/wiki/27th_parallel_north" title="27th parallel north">27°</a> and 36°N, and longitudes 1° and <a href="/wiki/14th_meridian_west" title="14th meridian west">14°W</a>. Adding Western Sahara, Morocco lies mostly between <a href="/wiki/21st_parallel_north" title="21st parallel north">21°</a> and <a href="/wiki/36th_parallel_north" title="36th parallel north">36°N</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1st_meridian_west" title="1st meridian west">1°</a> and <a href="/wiki/17th_meridian_west" title="17th meridian west">17°W</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Ras_Nouadhibou" title="Ras Nouadhibou">Ras Nouadhibou</a> peninsula is slightly south of 21° and west of 17°).
</p><p>The geography of Morocco spans from the Atlantic Ocean, to mountainous areas, to the Sahara desert. Morocco is a <a href="/wiki/Northern_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Africa">Northern African</a> country, bordering the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Ocean" class="mw-redirect" title="North Atlantic Ocean">North Atlantic Ocean</a> and the Mediterranean Sea, between Algeria and the annexed Western Sahara. It is one of only three nations (along with <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>) to have both Atlantic and Mediterranean coastlines.
</p><p>A large part of Morocco is mountainous. The <a href="/wiki/Atlas_Mountains" title="Atlas Mountains">Atlas Mountains</a> are located mainly in the centre and the south of the country. The <a href="/wiki/Rif_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Rif Mountains">Rif Mountains</a> are located in the north of the country. Both ranges are mainly inhabited by the <a href="/wiki/Berber_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Berber people">Berber people</a>. At 446,550&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (172,414&#160;sq&#160;mi), Morocco excluding Western Sahara is the fifty-seventh largest country in the world. Algeria borders Morocco to the east and southeast, though the border between the two countries has been closed since 1994.
</p><p>Spanish territory in Northwest Africa neighbouring Morocco comprises five enclaves on the Mediterranean coast: <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pe%C3%B1%C3%B3n_de_V%C3%A9lez_de_la_Gomera" title="Peñón de Vélez de la Gomera">Peñón de Vélez de la Gomera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pe%C3%B1%C3%B3n_de_Alhucemas" class="mw-redirect" title="Peñón de Alhucemas">Peñón de Alhucemas</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Islas_Chafarinas" class="mw-redirect" title="Islas Chafarinas">Chafarinas</a> islands, and the disputed islet <a href="/wiki/Isla_Perejil" class="mw-redirect" title="Isla Perejil">Perejil</a>. Off the Atlantic coast the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> belong to Spain, whereas <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> to the north is <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a>. To the north, Morocco is bordered by the Strait of Gibraltar, where international shipping has unimpeded <a href="/wiki/Transit_passage" title="Transit passage">transit passage</a> between the Atlantic and Mediterranean.
</p><p>The Rif mountains stretch over the region bordering the Mediterranean from the north-west to the north-east. The Atlas Mountains run down the backbone of the country,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> from the northeast to the southwest. Most of the southeast portion of the country is in the <a href="/wiki/Sahara_Desert" class="mw-redirect" title="Sahara Desert">Sahara Desert</a> and as such is generally sparsely populated and unproductive economically. Most of the population lives to the north of these mountains, while to the south lies the Western Sahara, a former Spanish colony that was annexed by Morocco in 1975 (see <a href="/wiki/Green_March" title="Green March">Green March</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-border_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-border-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Morocco claims that the Western Sahara is part of its territory and refers to that as its <a href="/wiki/Southern_Provinces" title="Southern Provinces">Southern Provinces</a>.
</p><p>Morocco's capital city is <a href="/wiki/Rabat" title="Rabat">Rabat</a>; its largest city is its main port, <a href="/wiki/Casablanca" title="Casablanca">Casablanca</a>. Other cities recording a population over 500,000 in the <a href="/wiki/2014_Moroccan_census" title="2014 Moroccan census">2014 Moroccan census</a> are <a href="/wiki/Fes" class="mw-redirect" title="Fes">Fes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marrakesh" title="Marrakesh">Marrakesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meknes" title="Meknes">Meknes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sal%C3%A9" title="Salé">Salé</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tangier" title="Tangier">Tangier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-moroccocensus2014_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moroccocensus2014-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Morocco is represented in the <a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-1_alpha-2" title="ISO 3166-1 alpha-2">ISO 3166-1 alpha-2</a> geographical encoding standard by the symbol <i>MA</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-ISO3166_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISO3166-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> This code was used as the basis for Morocco's internet domain, <a href="/wiki/.ma" title=".ma">.ma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ISO3166_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISO3166-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Morocco_K%C3%B6ppen.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Morocco_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/220px-Morocco_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="264" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Morocco_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/330px-Morocco_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Morocco_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/440px-Morocco_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="765" data-file-height="918" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Morocco_K%C3%B6ppen.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Köppen climate types in Morocco</div></div></div><p>The country's <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> is similar to that of southern <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, with lush forests in the northern and central mountain ranges of the country, giving way to drier conditions and inland deserts further southeast. The Moroccan coastal plains experience remarkably moderate temperatures even in summer, owing to the effect of the cold <a href="/wiki/Canary_Current" title="Canary Current">Canary Current</a> off its <a href="/wiki/Atlantic" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic">Atlantic</a> coast.
</p><p>In the Rif, Middle and High Atlas Mountains, there exist several different types of climates: Mediterranean along the coastal lowlands, giving way to a humid temperate climate at higher elevations with sufficient moisture to allow for the growth of different species of oaks, moss carpets, junipers, and Atlantic fir which is a royal conifer tree <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> to Morocco. In the valleys, fertile soils and high precipitation allow for the growth of thick and lush forests. Cloud forests can be found in the west of the Rif Mountains and Middle Atlas Mountains. At higher elevations, the climate becomes alpine in character, and can sustain ski resorts.
</p><p>Southeast of the Atlas mountains, near the Algerian borders, the climate becomes very dry, with long and hot summers. Extreme heat and low moisture levels are especially pronounced in the lowland regions east of the Atlas range due to the rain shadow effect of the mountain system. The southeastern-most portions of Morocco are very hot, and include portions of the <a href="/wiki/Sahara_Desert" class="mw-redirect" title="Sahara Desert">Sahara Desert</a>, where vast swathes of sand dunes and rocky plains are dotted with lush <a href="/wiki/Oasis" title="Oasis">oases</a>.
</p><p>In contrast to the Sahara region in the south, coastal <a href="/wiki/Plain" title="Plain">plains</a> are fertile in the central and northern regions of the country, and comprise the backbone of the country's agriculture, in which 95% of the population live. The direct exposure to the North Atlantic Ocean, the proximity to mainland Europe and the long stretched Rif and Atlas mountains are the factors of the rather European-like climate in the northern half of the country. That makes Morocco a country of contrasts. <a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">Forested areas</a> cover about 12% of the country while arable land accounts for 18%. Approximately 5% of Moroccan land is irrigated for agricultural use.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Merzouga_sahara.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Merzouga_sahara.jpg/220px-Merzouga_sahara.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Merzouga_sahara.jpg/330px-Merzouga_sahara.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Merzouga_sahara.jpg/440px-Merzouga_sahara.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2600" data-file-height="1733" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Merzouga_sahara.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Landscape of the <a href="/wiki/Erg_Chebbi" title="Erg Chebbi">Erg Chebbi</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Djebel_Toubkal_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Djebel_Toubkal_01.jpg/220px-Djebel_Toubkal_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Djebel_Toubkal_01.jpg/330px-Djebel_Toubkal_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Djebel_Toubkal_01.jpg/440px-Djebel_Toubkal_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Djebel_Toubkal_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Atlas_Mountains" title="Atlas Mountains">Atlas Mountains</a></div></div></div>
<p>In general, apart from the southeast regions (pre-Saharan and desert areas), Morocco's climate and geography are very similar to the Iberian peninsula. Thus Morocco has the following climate zones:
</p>
<ul><li><b>Mediterranean:</b> Dominates the coastal Mediterranean regions of the country, along the (500&#160;km strip), and some parts of the Atlantic coast. Summers are hot to moderately hot and dry, average highs are between 29&#160;°C (84.2&#160;°F) and 32&#160;°C (89.6&#160;°F). Winters are generally mild and wet, daily average temperatures hover around 9&#160;°C (48.2&#160;°F) to 11&#160;°C (51.8&#160;°F), and average low are around 5&#160;°C (41.0&#160;°F) to 8&#160;°C (46.4&#160;°F), typical to the coastal areas of the west Mediterranean. Annual Precipitation in this area vary from 600–800&#160;mm in the west to 350–500&#160;mm in the east. Notable cities that fall into this zone are <a href="/wiki/Tangier" title="Tangier">Tangier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tetouan" class="mw-redirect" title="Tetouan">Tetouan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Hoceima" title="Al Hoceima">Al Hoceima</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nador" title="Nador">Nador</a> and <a href="/wiki/Safi,_Morocco" title="Safi, Morocco">Safi</a>.</li>
<li><b>Sub-Mediterranean:</b> It influences cities that show Mediterranean characteristics, but remain fairly influenced by other climates owing to their either relative elevation, or direct exposure to the North Atlantic Ocean. We thus have two main influencing climates:</li></ul>
<dl><dd><ul><li><i>Oceanic:</i> Determined by the cooler summers, where highs are around 27&#160;°C (80.6&#160;°F) and in terms of the Essaouira region, are almost always around 21&#160;°C (69.8&#160;°F). The medium daily temperatures can get as low as 19&#160;°C (66.2&#160;°F), while winters are chilly to mild and wet. Annual precipitation varies from 400 to 700&#160;mm. Notable cities that fall into this zone are <a href="/wiki/Rabat" title="Rabat">Rabat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Casablanca" title="Casablanca">Casablanca</a>, <a href="/wiki/K%C3%A9nitra" class="mw-redirect" title="Kénitra">Kénitra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sal%C3%A9" title="Salé">Salé</a> and <a href="/wiki/Essaouira" title="Essaouira">Essaouira</a>.</li></ul></dd></dl>
<dl><dd><ul><li><i>Continental:</i> Determined by the bigger gap between highs and lows, that results in hotter summers and colder winters, than found in typical Mediterranean zones. In summer, daily highs can get as high as 40&#160;°C (104.0&#160;°F) during heat waves, but usually are between 32&#160;°C (89.6&#160;°F) and 36&#160;°C (96.8&#160;°F). However, temperatures drop as the sun sets. Night temperatures usually fall below 20&#160;°C (68.0&#160;°F), and sometimes as low as 10&#160;°C (50.0&#160;°F) in mid-summer. Winters are cooler, and can get below the freezing point multiple times between December and February. Also, snow can fall occasionally. Fès for example registered −8&#160;°C (17.6&#160;°F) in winter 2005. Annual precipitation varies between 500 and 900&#160;mm. Notable cities are <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A8s" class="mw-redirect" title="Fès">Fès</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mekn%C3%A8s" class="mw-redirect" title="Meknès">Meknès</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chefchaouen" title="Chefchaouen">Chefchaouen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beni-Mellal" class="mw-redirect" title="Beni-Mellal">Beni-Mellal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taza" title="Taza">Taza</a>.</li></ul></dd></dl>
<ul><li><b>Continental:</b> Dominates the mountainous regions of the north and central parts of the country, where summers are hot to very hot, with highs between 32&#160;°C (89.6&#160;°F) and 36&#160;°C (96.8&#160;°F). Winters on the other hand are cold, and lows usually go beyond the freezing point. And when cold damp air comes to Morocco from the northwest, for a few days, temperatures sometimes get below −5&#160;°C (23.0&#160;°F). It often snows abundantly in this part of the country. Precipitation varies between 400 and 800&#160;mm. Notable cities are <a href="/wiki/Khenifra" title="Khenifra">Khenifra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Imilchil" title="Imilchil">Imilchil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Midelt" title="Midelt">Midelt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Azilal" title="Azilal">Azilal</a>.</li>
<li><b>Alpine:</b> Found in some parts of the Middle Atlas Mountain range and the eastern part of the High Atlas Mountain range. Summers are very warm to moderately hot, and winters are longer, cold and snowy. Precipitation varies between 400 and 1200&#160;mm. In summer highs barely go above 30&#160;°C (86.0&#160;°F), and lows are cool and average below 15&#160;°C (59.0&#160;°F). In winters, highs average around 8&#160;°C (46.4&#160;°F), and lows go well below the freezing point. In this part of country, there are many ski resorts, such as Oukaimeden and Mischliefen. Notable cities are <a href="/wiki/Ifrane" title="Ifrane">Ifrane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azrou" title="Azrou">Azrou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boulmane" class="mw-redirect" title="Boulmane">Boulmane</a>.</li>
<li><b>Semi-arid:</b> This type of climate is found in the south of the country and some parts of the east of the country, where rainfall is lower and annual precipitations are between 200 and 350&#160;mm. However, one usually finds Mediterranean characteristics in those regions, such as the precipitation pattern and thermal attributes. Notable cities are <a href="/wiki/Agadir" title="Agadir">Agadir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marrakesh" title="Marrakesh">Marrakesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oujda" title="Oujda">Oujda</a>.</li></ul>
<p>South of Agadir and east of Jerada near the Algerian borders, arid and desert climate starts to prevail.
</p><p>Due to Morocco's proximity to the Sahara desert and the North Sea of the Atlantic Ocean, two phenomena occur to influence the regional seasonal temperatures, either by raising temperatures by 7–8 degrees Celsius when <a href="/wiki/Sirocco" title="Sirocco">sirocco</a> blows from the east creating heatwaves, or by lowering temperatures by 7–8 degrees Celsius when cold damp air blows from the northwest, creating a coldwave or cold spell. However, these phenomena do not last for more than two to five days on average.
</p><p>Countries or regions that share the same climatic characteristics with Morocco are the state of <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> (USA), <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Precipitation">Precipitation</span></h4>
<p>Annual rainfall in Morocco is different according to regions. The northwestern parts of the country receive between 500&#160;mm and 1200&#160;mm, while the northeastern parts receive between 350 and 600&#160;mm. North Central Morocco receives between 700&#160;mm and up to 3500&#160;mm. The area from Casablanca to Essaouira, on the Atlantic coast, receives between 300&#160;mm and 500&#160;mm. The regions from Essaouira to Agadir receive between 250&#160;mm and 400&#160;mm. Marrakesh region in the central south receives only 250&#160;mm a year. The southeastern regions, basically the driest areas, receive between 100&#160;mm and 200&#160;mm only, and consist basically of arid and desert lands.
</p><p>Botanically speaking, Morocco enjoys a great variety of vegetation, from lush large forests of conifer and oak trees typical of the western Mediterranean countries (Morocco, Algeria, Italy, Spain, France and Portugal), to shrubs and acacias further south. This is due to the diversity of climate and the precipitation patterns in the country.
</p><p>Morocco's weather is one of the most pristine in terms of the four-season experience. Most regions have distinct seasons where summer is usually not spoiled by rain and winter turns wet, snowy and humid with mild, cool to cold temperatures, while spring and fall see warm to mild weather characterised by flowers blooming in spring and falling leaves in autumn. This type of weather has affected the Moroccan culture and behaviour and played a part in the social interaction of the population, like many other countries that fall into this type of climate zone.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_a_father.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Portrait_of_a_father.jpg/240px-Portrait_of_a_father.jpg" decoding="async" width="240" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Portrait_of_a_father.jpg/360px-Portrait_of_a_father.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Portrait_of_a_father.jpg/480px-Portrait_of_a_father.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1170" data-file-height="900" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_a_father.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An adult male <a href="/wiki/Barbary_macaque" title="Barbary macaque">Barbary macaque</a> carrying his offspring, a behaviour rarely found in other primates.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barbary_lion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Barbary_lion.jpg/240px-Barbary_lion.jpg" decoding="async" width="240" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Barbary_lion.jpg/360px-Barbary_lion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Barbary_lion.jpg/480px-Barbary_lion.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2604" data-file-height="1776" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barbary_lion.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Barbary_lion" title="Barbary lion">Barbary lion</a></div></div></div>
<p>Morocco has a wide range of <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>.
